  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f5f443b5-9b75-498f-ab47-8d2c5411e2b9'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText718393812666582545" style="display:none">A new realm of magic from Emily Rodda, the New York Times bestselling author of the Deltora books.<br /><br />There are three rules to the old painted, music box: Wind the box three times only. Never shut the box when the music is playing. Never move the box before the music stops.<br /><br />Leo wouldn't dream of breaking these rules, but does his stubborn cousin Mimi listen? She winds the box four times -- and suddenly the paintings on its side come to life and a powerful witch is released. Now its up to Leo and Mimi to stop the witch, if only they can find the key to the music box -- and the magical world it controls.</span>

<div id="review_41962967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41962967" />
    <a title="Eva Mitnick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/633929-eva-mitnick"><img alt="Eva Mitnick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237933117p2/633929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41962967?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eva Mitnick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eva Mitnick" href="/user/show/633929-eva-mitnick">Eva Mitnick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/633929-eva-mitnick?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/633929-eva-mitnick?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41962967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13157177100738482341">At first glance, this sounds like dozens (and probably hundreds) of other fantasy novels for children. Two mismatched kids figure out a way into a magical realm and are immediately in danger. They set out on a quest, during which they meet many fascinating denizens of the realm and learn much about themselves and each other. Ultimately, all ends well.<br/><br/>This happens to a genre that is as delicious to me as strawberries with cream. Whether it’s the Narnia books, Alice in Wonderland, or the many cont</span>
  <span id="freeText13157177100738482341" style="display:none">At first glance, this sounds like dozens (and probably hundreds) of other fantasy novels for children. Two mismatched kids figure out a way into a magical realm and are immediately in danger. They set out on a quest, during which they meet many fascinating denizens of the realm and learn much about themselves and each other. Ultimately, all ends well.<br /><br />This happens to a genre that is as delicious to me as strawberries with cream. Whether it’s the Narnia books, Alice in Wonderland, or the many contemporary examples of the genre, there is something about strangers in a strange land that gets the creative and imaginative juices flowing.<br /><br />Luckily, The Key to Rondo happens to be an especially fine example of this type of fantasy. It has Rules That Must Not Be Broken (all pertaining to an old painted music box, which happens also to be the alternate world), as well as logical repercussions when these rules are broken. Strange and ominous occurrences in early chapters receive surprising explanations by the end of the book. Characters and plot work together in the most satisfying way.<br /><br />Leo and Mimi are the two children who are plunged into this world when Mimi (a rather disagreeable child a la Eustace Scrubb from The Voyage of the Dawn Treader or – to use a non-fantasy example – Mary Lennox from The Secret Garden) insists on breaking the first rule of the music box that Leo (a risk-averse, obedient child) has just inherited from his aunt. Instead of stopping at three turns, Mimi winds it four times, which allows a nasty witch from the music box world to enter their own world. This witch steals Mimi’s beloved dog, forcing Mimi (and thus a reluctant Leo) to enter the music box world to get him back.<br /><br />Neither Mimi nor Leo become different people – flaws and quirks thankfully remain in place – but their quest brings them greater understanding and appreciation of each other and allows them to grow, as every good quest must. They meet a variety of human, animal, and fantastical creatures, many of whom are based on familiar fairy tale characters (a bit like Rapunzel’s Revenge by Shannon Hale, Into the Woods by Lyn Gardner, and many other similar fantasies). However, these characters are complex and interesting folks in their own right and never once come across as undeveloped or stock.<br /><br />Danger, treachery, misunderstanding, and plenty of magic and humor combine to make this a thrilling and engrossing fantasy for grades 4 – 8.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13157177100738482341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText12193903074776348159" style="display:none">The Key To Rondo is the newest title from Australian author Emily Rodda (Rowan of Rin series). When Leo Zifkak inherits his Aunt Bethany's elaborately decorated music box he takes the rules posted on the bottom seriously - only wind it up three turns, never pick it up while its playing. His cousin, Mimi, on the other hand is a little less of a conformist and winds the box four times. Butterflies come alive from one panel of paintings. This is the same high quality fantasy for middles grade readers that Rodda perfected with the Rowan series. Recommend The Key to Rondo to fantasy readers who enjoy quick pacing, clever plot, and unique characters. </span>

<div id="review_1989077121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1989077121" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1989077121?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545103817" href="/book/show/10538830-the-key-to-rondo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy-fairytale">fantasy-fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1989077121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer388182777464476949">First in the Rondo fantastical fairytale adventure series for eight-to-eleven-year-old middle-grade readers and revolving around the adventure-seeking Langlander family, and more specifically Leo and Mimi.<br/><br/>In 2008, <em>The Key to Rondo</em> won the Kids Own Australian Literature Awards (KOALA) for Older Readers.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>Right off, I didn't like Mimi. In fact, I wanted to slap her upside the head. Rude. Inconsiderate. Stubborn. Snotty. And then you learn more about her.<br/><br/>There are multiple levels in here that </span>
  <span id="freeText388182777464476949" style="display:none">First in the Rondo fantastical fairytale adventure series for eight-to-eleven-year-old middle-grade readers and revolving around the adventure-seeking Langlander family, and more specifically Leo and Mimi.<br /><br />In 2008, <em>The Key to Rondo</em> won the Kids Own Australian Literature Awards (KOALA) for Older Readers.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Right off, I didn't like Mimi. In fact, I wanted to slap her upside the head. Rude. Inconsiderate. Stubborn. Snotty. And then you learn more about her.<br /><br />There are multiple levels in here that will stimulate the kids, especially if they've been reading their fairy tales. I love how Rodda has twined [so many of] them in. As for tension, there's just the right amount for the young'uns and part of what keeps events smooth is Rodda's use of third-person subjective point-of-view, as the narrator keeps us informed on everyone's thoughts.<br /><br />I do like the idea of the red hooks, and lol, the thought that clothes don't want to be worn by someone who'd make them look ugly! I mean, really…!<br /><br />The gingerbread men served at tea seem to foreshadow the world of Rondo. I never thought of them as pests before, though. Well, maybe to my waistline.<br /><br />That ending was not what I expected, a nice twist on that "happy ending" trope, lol. Such a blatant — and great — excuse to keep going *more laughter* Seems I'll have to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5155532-the-wizard-of-rondo" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Wizard of Rondo</em>
</a>.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />The music box has been in the Langlander family for centuries, and Leo is its new owner. And much more conscientious than his annoying, rule-breaking cousin!<br /><br />It's a rude introduction to Rondo, and worse when they hear the Langlander tales from Grandma. It's not just a matter of rescuing Mutt from the evil queen, but freeing this world from what their ancestors have done.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br />Young <strong>Leo Zifkak</strong> has a fascination for woodworking, that no one encourages. <br /><strong>Tony Zifkak</strong>, a scientist who prefers the comfortable refuge of his home, and <strong>Suzanne Langlander</strong> are his parents. <strong>Einstein</strong> is their black cat.<br /><br />Marion "<strong>Mimi</strong>" Langlander, a brilliant violinist, is his least-favorite second cousin; her own family doesn't know what (or want anything) to do with her. <strong>Mutt</strong> is Mimi's persnickety dog. <strong>Aunt Carol and Uncle Robert</strong> are her parents heading off on vacation. Her siblings (and their spouses??) include <strong>Chris</strong> and <strong>Kwon</strong> and <strong>Martin</strong> and <strong>Monique</strong>.<br /><br /><em>Rondo is…</em><br />…the world around the music box. <strong>Crumble</strong> is the pie man. <strong>Posy</strong> is the flower seller. <strong>Officer Begood</strong> is the local copper. Old <strong>Jolly</strong> runs the <strong>Black Sheep</strong> inn. The vain <strong>Bertha</strong> is Jolly's much-painted pig with hidden strengths. <em>Seems Jolly took the art gallery owner's advice (<strong>Monsieur Rouge-et-Noir</strong>) the wrong way, lol.</em> Bertha actually works as a watch pig on Jolly's brother's farm, <strong>Farmer Jack Macdonald</strong>; <strong>Mary</strong> is the farmer's wife. <strong>Dolly and Teddy</strong> run a toy factory. <strong>Master Whitebeard</strong> has had his wallet stolen. <strong>Pop</strong> sells balloons.<br /><br /><strong>Freda</strong> is the dot-eating duck partnered up with <strong>Conker</strong>, a dot eradicator.<br /><br /><strong>Rosebud</strong> is <strong>Jim</strong> the woodcutter and <strong>Polly</strong> (who used to wear a red hood when visiting Grandma)'s baby. They both live with <strong>Grandma</strong> outside the village. In the woods. <strong>Rufus</strong> is their dot-eating fox. <strong>Charlie</strong> had been Grandma's fiddle-playing cat while <strong>Arthur</strong> had been her husband. Jim's father had been a personal guard for the queen; <strong>Lily</strong> and <strong>Suki</strong> had been Jim's sisters [well, Suki was more of a foster-sister] who married <strong>Walter</strong>. They're all swans now. Seven of 'em.<br /><br /><strong>Hal</strong> is the great wizard who broke the queen's power…and broke his own as well.<br /><br /><strong>Flitter Wood</strong> is where <strong>Tye</strong>, a <strong>Terlamaine</strong> (tiger woman), lives as do the <strong>Flitters</strong>, bright green little fairies, who live in the Nesting Tree. <strong>Hobnob</strong> is where <strong>Old Wizard Bing</strong> lives.<br /><br /><strong>Dots</strong> are pests who happen to look like gingerbread men, right down to the two currant eyes and three currant buttons. <strong>Hidey-holes</strong> are sentient and provide you with, well, a hidey-hole when you need it. <strong>Mice</strong> act as messengers (which reminds me of Angie Sage's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/44897-septimus-heap" title="Opens a list of books in Angie Sage's Septimus Heap series in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Septimus Heap</a>). <strong>Gaps</strong> appear to be tunnels through space that shorten the distance between locations.<br /><br />The <strong>Blue Queen</strong>'s power was broken and the <strong>Dark Time</strong> ended. <strong>Tom Spoiler</strong> is a sneak of a thief who is/was in league with the queen.<br /><br /><em>The Langlanders</em><br /><strong>Aunt Bethany Langlander</strong> had been the last holder of the music box. <em>And it sounds as if she had a very boring life, dying at 94 in front of the telly.</em> <strong>Mr. Higgs</strong> had been her gardener and handyman. <strong>Monty and Ida Langlander</strong> had been Aunt Bethany's great-grandparents. <strong>Rollo</strong> is a long-ago ancestor who had brought the box back from his travels. <strong>Alice Langlander</strong> had played the harp and ran off to join a circus. <strong>Wicked Uncle George Langlander</strong> was the family disgrace. <strong>Uncle Henry</strong> had been the responsible one who drowned three days after he retired from the bank.<br /><br /><b>The Cover and Title</b><br />The cover is just plain scary with Tye looking like an evil cat warrior in black leather corset with studded cap sleeves and studded leather gauntlets, reaching for the sword at her side and leaning up against a huge tree, its ribbed gray bark providing excellent contrast for the bright green winged Flitters flittering around her. The title is in an embossed gold at the top with swirls curling around the end of the "R" and a scroll of leaves waving out from the tip of the "Y".<br /><br />The title is the true focus of the story, <em>The Key to Rondo</em>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="388182777464476949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4901382685686330891">The Key to Rondo by Emily Rodda is a fantasy book which starts from an old music box with strict rules that has been given to Leo through the Langlander. <br/><br/>Important!<br/><br/>Turn the key three times only<br/>Never turn the key while the music is playing<br/>Never pick up the box while the music is playing <br/>Never close the lid until the music has stopped <br/><br/>The box is painted with villages, mysterious forest, a castle on a hill and a queen in along blue gown, known as the Blue Queen. The main characters in the book are </span>
  <span id="freeText4901382685686330891" style="display:none">The Key to Rondo by Emily Rodda is a fantasy book which starts from an old music box with strict rules that has been given to Leo through the Langlander. <br /><br />Important!<br /><br />Turn the key three times only<br />Never turn the key while the music is playing<br />Never pick up the box while the music is playing <br />Never close the lid until the music has stopped <br /><br />The box is painted with villages, mysterious forest, a castle on a hill and a queen in along blue gown, known as the Blue Queen. The main characters in the book are Leo who is a shy and timid person who follows the rules while his cousin Mimi is the total opposite but has a secretive. A key theme is trust as throughout the book the characters need to depend on each other and trust each other to not fall into deeper trouble. I personally thought that it was quite a nice to book to read. I liked how there were many unexpected turns. I would recommend this book to anyone who enjoy an adventure book mixed with fantasy and friendship. :)</span>

<div id="review_1127915979" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127915979" />
    <a title="Raymond Xu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35094681-raymond-xu"><img alt="Raymond Xu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411159313p2/35094681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127915979?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raymond Xu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raymond Xu" href="/user/show/35094681-raymond-xu">Raymond Xu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127915979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14915835595196254021">The reason why I was reading this book was because I didn't have any other books to read. Although I've bought this book, I've never read it because the cover doesn't look really interesting. So I decided to start reading this. Mimi and Leo were cousins and Mimi was the dark-sided trouble maker. Leo was honest and responsible. One day Mimi decided to turn the music box(Rondo) more than three times(the generations of longlanders were told not to wind it more than three times). The blue queen took</span>
  <span id="freeText14915835595196254021" style="display:none">The reason why I was reading this book was because I didn't have any other books to read. Although I've bought this book, I've never read it because the cover doesn't look really interesting. So I decided to start reading this. Mimi and Leo were cousins and Mimi was the dark-sided trouble maker. Leo was honest and responsible. One day Mimi decided to turn the music box(Rondo) more than three times(the generations of longlanders were told not to wind it more than three times). The blue queen took Mimi's dog and that's when Mimi and Leo decided to go to Rondo to save the dog.<br />Theme: <br />I think that the theme for this book is to be wary of whom you're talking to. Since Leo and Mimi were in a hurry to find Mutt (dog) they trusted anyone they can which led to consequences. Sometimes they were too cautious and over think things when someone is helping them. Too much wariness can cause betrayal and sometimes even worse. In the text it states, "We thought you were writing to the Blue Queen. The mouse was so scared" (324). This reveals that if you worry too much it can have good or bad effects. <br />I learn from this book that you should be careful to who you are talking to and not break any rules.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14915835595196254021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648359728" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648359728?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=fairyly-good-tales-myth-adventures">fairyly-good-tales-myth-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=the-price-of-magic">the-price-of-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=world-inside-a-world">world-inside-a-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9577006-h?shelf=villains-are-my-fave">villains-are-my-fave</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648359728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14286093559115034271">So cute, so cute, so cute!! This book had a little inception going on-- this secret music box world within our own much bigger and more complex world. I love all the books that Emily Rodda writes because to me, they have a sort of whimsy and uniqueness to them. This definitely does not disappoint.<br/> I was a little hesitant to read it, but I was on a long 14 hour road trip, so I wasn't about to complain when my sister handed me some reading material to divert my mind from the boredom.<br/> All in all, i</span>
  <span id="freeText14286093559115034271" style="display:none">So cute, so cute, so cute!! This book had a little inception going on-- this secret music box world within our own much bigger and more complex world. I love all the books that Emily Rodda writes because to me, they have a sort of whimsy and uniqueness to them. This definitely does not disappoint.<br /> I was a little hesitant to read it, but I was on a long 14 hour road trip, so I wasn't about to complain when my sister handed me some reading material to divert my mind from the boredom.<br /> All in all, it's a cute read. Rodda puts in some awesome imagery details that really help the reader imagine the world as she did. Ah, yes the world building is fairly intricate for the intended audience. I was in heaven!! And inexplicably, I was drawn to Spoiler. His character as the bad guy really just intrigued me, more so than the main villain, the Blue Queen. And I loved Hal!!! So much!! All the characters were very likable and original. Definitely worth a shot reading to all you out there!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14286093559115034271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180043211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13763652486126083884">This was a cute story and a fast. Leo inherits a beautifully hand-painted music box that comes with very specific rules about how many times to wind it and when it can be moved. Leo is determined to follow these rules but when his cousin Mimi comes to visit she thinks the rules are stupid. What they discover is that those rules were designed to keep the world inside the music box a secret. When the rules are broken people and creatures from this world can come out and people from Leo and Mimi's </span>
  <span id="freeText13763652486126083884" style="display:none">This was a cute story and a fast. Leo inherits a beautifully hand-painted music box that comes with very specific rules about how many times to wind it and when it can be moved. Leo is determined to follow these rules but when his cousin Mimi comes to visit she thinks the rules are stupid. What they discover is that those rules were designed to keep the world inside the music box a secret. When the rules are broken people and creatures from this world can come out and people from Leo and Mimi's world can go in.<br /><br />When Mimi breaks turns the key too many times the Blue Queen comes out and kidnaps Mimi's dog Mutt. Mimi is determined to get him back and goes in after him. Poor Leo is dragged along for the ride. What follows is a fun little story about their adventures as they learn who to trust and who is not worthy of trust.<br /><br />I'll definitely be continuing on to Book 2.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13763652486126083884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The music box was a treasured family heirloom. The music that played when the lid was opened was almost hypnotic. But unlike most music boxes this one had 4 rules.<br/><br/><br/>“Turn the key three times only.<br/>Never turn the key while the music is playing.<br/>Never pick up the box while the music is playing.<br/>Never close the lid until the music has stopped.”<br/><br/>Why these ru</span>
  <span id="freeText9037010961383435253" style="display:none">Rodda, Emily The Key to Rondo, 333pgs. Scholastic Press; Language~G, Sexual Content~G; Violence~G; When Aunt Bethany died she left Leo her music box. The music box was a treasured family heirloom. The music that played when the lid was opened was almost hypnotic. But unlike most music boxes this one had 4 rules.<br /><br /><br />“Turn the key three times only.<br />Never turn the key while the music is playing.<br />Never pick up the box while the music is playing.<br />Never close the lid until the music has stopped.”<br /><br />Why these rules existed, Leo didn’t know. The sides and top of the music box was painted with various scenes all which Leo knew by heart from the many times he had studied the box. Leo’s life changed the day his cousin Mimi turned the key four times! Characters from the music box came alive into the room! First it was blue butterflies, but the next time it was a beautiful lady all dressed in blue. Little did they know that the lady was an evil queen with evil intentions for Leo and Mimi. The evil queen kidnaps Mimi’s dog and returns to the music box. Mimi insists that they follow and thus begins Leo’s adventure in the land of Rondo.<br /><br />Emily Rodda has once again created a fabulous fantasy tale for young readers to lose themselves in. This story would make an excellent class read-a-loud.<br /><br />EL, MS - ESSENTIAL. Allison Madsen~Teen Librarian-SJO Public Librarian<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://kissthebook.blogspot.com/2008/09/rodda-emily-key-to-rondo-333pgs.html">http://kissthebook.blogspot.com/2008/...</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11963439085683276394">Emily Rodda’s style is reminiscent of Dyiana Wynne Jones, though with less whimsy, not quite as much chaos, and a smidge more mystery.<br/>Leo was a wonderful POV character, whose reactions to first entering a fantasy world were understandable and not overdone. He strives to do the right thing even when it’s difficult, and does a decent job of it to boot. He’s the perfect balance to his head-strong cousin Mimi, who loves to question and test the rules (as well as figuring them out for herself).<br/><br/>The si</span>
  <span id="freeText11963439085683276394" style="display:none">Emily Rodda’s style is reminiscent of Dyiana Wynne Jones, though with less whimsy, not quite as much chaos, and a smidge more mystery.<br />Leo was a wonderful POV character, whose reactions to first entering a fantasy world were understandable and not overdone. He strives to do the right thing even when it’s difficult, and does a decent job of it to boot. He’s the perfect balance to his head-strong cousin Mimi, who loves to question and test the rules (as well as figuring them out for herself).<br /><br />The side characters were a wonderful blend of clashing temperaments; the steady Jim, the mysterious and somewhat woeful Hal, the boisterous Conker, the fiery Freda, the vain and heroic Bertha...the list goes on!<br /><br />The music-box world of magic, fairy tale characters, talking animals, cat-people, and wild gingerbread men all made for a fun and sometimes terrifying (for the characters) blend (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ah, and that genocide of the cat-people at the hands of the Blue Queen, there’s that...it’s mentioned and there is one left, but genocide happened in Rondo. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<br /><br />This is the first book in the series, but it stood on its own and left the ending open for a sequel without leaving any loose threads.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64752900-madeline-o-rourke?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2163462245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2692451066046117382">As far as middle grade fantasies go, <i>The Key to Rondo</i> is solid. I've read better—and I've read better from Rodda—but it shows a lot of promise for the sequels.<br/><br/>The novel itself is very repetitive in terms of the protagonists mistrusting other characters, betrayals, red herrings, etc. Certain plot reveals or revelations made by the protagonists were also massively oversimplified, and though I could predict them, it did not feel realistic to have the characters suddenly realise these things. Howeve</span>
  <span id="freeText2692451066046117382" style="display:none">As far as middle grade fantasies go, <i>The Key to Rondo</i> is solid. I've read better—and I've read better from Rodda—but it shows a lot of promise for the sequels.<br /><br />The novel itself is very repetitive in terms of the protagonists mistrusting other characters, betrayals, red herrings, etc. Certain plot reveals or revelations made by the protagonists were also massively oversimplified, and though I could predict them, it did not feel realistic to have the characters suddenly realise these things. However, I am also reading this with the eyes of an adult. I really did like the protagonists, especially Mimi's strength of character. <br /><br />The world itself is interesting and really developed as the story went on. I love all the little references to myriad fairytales, and I'm keen to see what pops up in the sequels. The overall history of the world may be a little cliche—and very Narnia-Esque—but I think that actually fits quite well with the whole idea of fairytales. <br /><br />Eager to see where the series leads!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2692451066046117382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16659987012655686246">I was lucky to stumble upon this series by accidentally picking up the second book— which I thought was a standalone.<br/><br/>This story, full of magic and happiness, takes you away to the world of Rondo.     <a title="Evelyn Lewis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83739422-evelyn-lewis"><img alt="Evelyn Lewis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546240481p2/83739422.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelyn Lewis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelyn Lewis" href="/user/show/83739422-evelyn-lewis">Evelyn Lewis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2793585883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3140652996369855152">Unoriginal premise. Uninspired characters. Tedious plot. Dull prose. This is what I remember when I tried, desperately, to read this, and I absolutely could not get into it. And I love fantasy stories about children finding strange new worlds. But there was absolutely nothing about this book that promised anything new or original. The characters were one-dimensional and bland. It was boring as heck. Don't know if I'd try anything else by Rodda.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0NvY51WnX0TFwiop1kI8qxzh3yP1rFClp3h+OdeLzLaUzvm4JysCl8GMvL8f3QFVsNmvRHsLEHP6AKQAvuNkEw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hL+K9Bm1uNUnQoKVeQMocBUgii8DTLUHeO4HVDvdyFrAqquraznlBiMMFAOwnBWOuRj6SI3r9dEllt1tUrVg/w==')})
  }

Moving into a publishing career, first as a book editor, and finally as a publisher at Angus & Robertson, Rodda's first book was published in 1984.</span>
